2:25:1398:0:14:72:435:700:12:Times:12:Times:C:Immigration to the U.S.:  A problem for the Republicans or the Democrats?
2:26:1471:14:14:72:350:686:12:Times:12:Times:C:Anna Maria Mayda, Giovanni Peri, and Walter Steingress
2:27:1525:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:C:NBER Working Paper No. 21941
2:28:1553:14:14:72:136:658:12:Times:12:Times:C:January 2016
2:29:1565:14:28:72:156:644:12:Times:12:Times:C:JEL No. F22,Z28
2:30:1580:28:28:306:339:616:12:Times:12:Times:C:ABSTRACT
2:31:1588:28:14:72:540:588:12:Times:12:Times:C:We empirically analyze the impact of immigration to the U.S. on the share of votes to the Republicans
2:32:1689:14:14:72:540:574:12:Times:12:Times:C:and Democrats between 1994 and 2012. Our analysis is based on variation across states and years
2:33:1784:14:14:72:540:560:12:Times:12:Times:C:– using data from the Current Population Survey merged with election data – and addresses the endogeneity
2:34:1889:14:14:72:540:546:12:Times:12:Times:C:of immigrant flows using a novel set of instruments. On average across election types, immigration
2:35:1987:14:14:72:540:532:12:Times:12:Times:C:to the U.S. has a significant and negative impact on the Republican vote share, consistent with the
2:36:2086:14:14:72:540:518:12:Times:12:Times:C:typical view of political analysts in the U.S. This average effect – which is driven by elections in the
2:37:2190:14:14:72:540:504:12:Times:12:Times:C:House – works through two main channels. The impact of immigration on Republican votes in the
2:38:2283:14:14:72:540:490:12:Times:12:Times:C:House is negative when the share of naturalized migrants in the voting population increases. Yet, it
2:39:2383:14:14:72:540:476:12:Times:12:Times:C:can be positive when the share of non-citizen migrants out of the population goes up and the size of
2:40:2483:14:14:72:540:462:12:Times:12:Times:C:migration makes it a salient policy issue in voters' minds. These results are consistent with naturalized
2:41:2588:14:14:72:540:448:12:Times:12:Times:C:migrants being less likely to vote for the Republican party than native voters and with native voters'
2:42:2690:14:14:72:540:434:12:Times:12:Times:C:political preferences moving towards the Republican party because of high immigration of non-citizens.
2:43:2792:14:42:72:510:420:12:Times:12:Times:C:This second effect, however, is significant only for very high levels of immigrant presence.
2:44:2884:42:14:72:166:378:12:Times:12:Times:C:Anna Maria Mayda
2:45:2900:14:14:72:215:364:12:Times:12:Times:C:Dept. of Economics, ICC 552
2:46:2927:14:14:72:185:350:12:Times:12:Times:C:Georgetown University
2:47:2948:14:14:72:187:336:12:Times:12:Times:C:37th and O Streets, NW
2:48:2970:14:14:72:186:322:12:Times:12:Times:C:Washington, DC 20057
2:49:2990:14:28:72:202:308:12:Times:12:Times:C:amm223@georgetown.edu
2:50:3011:28:14:72:139:280:12:Times:12:Times:C:Giovanni Peri
2:51:3024:14:14:72:198:266:12:Times:12:Times:C:Department of Economics
2:52:3047:14:14:72:221:252:12:Times:12:Times:C:University of California, Davis
2:53:3078:14:14:72:171:238:12:Times:12:Times:C:One Shields Avenue
2:54:3096:14:14:72:156:224:12:Times:12:Times:C:Davis, CA 95616
2:55:3111:14:14:72:124:210:12:Times:12:Times:C:and NBER

3:62:3253:0:15:121:491:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:“...  the enormous flow of legal immigrants to the country has remade and
3:63:3326:15:14:121:491:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:continues  to  remake  the  nation’s  electorate  in  favor  of  the  Democratic
3:64:3406:14:15:121:491:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:Party.”(Center for Immigration Studies (CIS) Background by James G.
3:65:3473:15:19:121:224:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:Gimpel, April 2014)
3:66:3492:19:15:121:491:622:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:“Many white Americans see that America is changing, believe that immi-
3:67:3562:15:14:121:491:607:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:gration is driving many of the negative changes and know that one party
3:68:3633:14:15:121:491:593:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:stands  largely  on  the  side  of  immigrants  while  the  other  party  stands
3:69:3713:15:14:121:491:578:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:largely in opposition.  For many whites, this is a powerful motivation to
3:70:3786:14:40:121:486:564:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:vote Republican.”(New York Times Op Ed article, November 20, 2014)
3:71:3852:40:26:91:227:524:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:1    Introduction
3:72:3869:26:15:91:519:498:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:The  topic  of  international  migration  and  its  consequences  frequently  occupies  the
3:73:3960:15:14:91:519:483:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:headlines of newspapers and television news shows in many rich countries.  Political
3:74:4044:14:15:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:leaders’ stand vis-a-vis this issue can be a very important determinant of their elec-
3:75:4130:15:14:91:519:454:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:toral success or failure.  In the United States the presidential debates have focussed
3:76:4216:14:14:91:519:440:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:over time on all issues related to migration – ranging from illegal migrants to the birth
3:77:4305:14:15:91:519:426:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:right to citizenship.  That migration has a defining effect on political outcomes has
3:78:4390:15:14:91:519:411:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:already been pointed out in the literature (see for example Ortega (2005) and other
3:79:4473:14:15:91:519:397:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:works discussed in Section 2) and, as noted above, is definitely taken into account
3:80:4556:15:14:91:519:382:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:by politicians.  Yet, to our knowledge, no study relative to the U.S. case has looked
3:81:4641:14:15:91:519:368:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:directly and systematically at one crucial aspect of the political effect of immigrants,
3:82:4729:15:14:91:519:353:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:namely their impact on the U.S. election outcomes and specifically on the share of
3:83:4811:14:15:91:519:339:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:votes to the two main political parties (Republicans and Democrats).1Against this
3:84:4892:15:14:91:519:324:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:background, this paper contributes to the literature by analyzing the link between
3:85:4974:14:15:91:519:310:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:migration to the U.S. and the vote share for the Republican and Democratic parties
3:86:5056:15:14:91:519:295:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:in every election between 1994 and 2012.  To that goal, we exploit the large variation
3:87:5142:14:14:91:519:281:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:in  immigration  across  states  and  years  and  the  corresponding  electoral  outcomes.
3:88:5232:14:15:91:519:267:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:We use data from the Current Population Survey merged with the National Library
3:89:5311:15:14:91:519:252:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of Congress Election data and, relying on a new identification strategy, we estimate
3:90:5395:14:29:91:457:238:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the causal effect of immigrants on the share of votes to the two parties.
3:91:5468:29:15:109:520:209:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:The number and share of immigrants in the U.S. adult population and labor force
3:92:5547:15:17:91:519:194:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:have been rising steadily over the last four decades.  Based on data from the U.S.
3:93:5629:17:16:105:519:177:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:1The only exception is a recent paper, Baerg et al. (2014), which estimates a negative impact of
3:94:5725:16:12:91:519:161:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:the share of unauthorized workers on the proportion of votes going to the Democrats in the U.S.
3:95:5820:12:0:91:302:149:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:state of Georgia, using variation across counties.
4:96:5871:0:15:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Census, there were 6.2 million foreign-born adults in the labor force in the U.S. (7.1
4:97:5957:15:14:91:519:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:percent of that group) in 1980, their number grew to 10.3 million (10.1 percent) in
4:98:6040:14:15:91:519:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:1990,  to  15.6  million  (14.4  percent)  in  2000  and  to  22.4  million  (19.1  percent)  in
4:99:6136:15:14:91:520:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:2010.2Given its magnitude, immigration to the U.S. is likely to have sizable effects
4:100:6220:14:15:91:519:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:on  its  economy  and  society,  through  several  different  channels.   Immigrants  may
4:101:6309:15:14:91:519:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:affect native workers’ opportunities in the labor market, as investigated by a large
4:102:6393:14:15:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:literature (see, for example the book by Borjas (2014) and the surveys by Blau and
4:103:6475:15:14:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Kahn (2012) and Lewis and Peri (2014) as overviews of this literature).  Immigrants
4:104:6558:14:15:91:519:569:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:are  also  likely  to  impact  the  destination  country’s  government  budget,  by  paying
4:105:6649:15:14:91:519:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:taxes, receiving public welfare and transfers and using public goods (see for instance
4:106:6735:14:14:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Edmonston et al. (1997) and Boeri et al. (2002)).  In addition, the literature points
4:107:6820:14:15:91:519:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:out several potential social effects of immigration on culture,  social norms and on
4:108:6904:15:14:91:520:511:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:crime and security3.  Finally, immigrants can also produce political changes in the
4:109:6987:14:15:91:519:497:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:destination country. The impact through the political channel is very important since
4:110:7072:15:14:91:519:482:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:it has the potential to affect the democratic support for institutions and policies in
4:111:7158:14:29:91:427:468:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the destination country and hence to produce long lasting effects.
4:112:7224:29:15:109:520:439:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:One  crucial  element  to  understand  the  effect  of  immigrants  on  vote  shares  is
4:113:7312:15:14:91:519:424:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:to  recognize  that  election  outcomes  can  be  affected  by  immigration  through  two
4:114:7401:14:14:91:519:410:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:channels, captured by the presence of two different groups of immigrants.  The first
4:115:7485:14:15:91:519:396:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:channel  is  related  to  the  indirect  political  effect  of  immigration  working  through
4:116:7578:15:14:91:520:381:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f6:B:migrants’ impact on existing voters, who are mainly natives.  It is voters’perceived
4:117:7662:14:15:91:519:367:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:impact of immigrants that affects how they cast their vote – and this perceived effect
4:118:7748:15:14:91:519:352:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:is likely to be stronger the more numerous migrants are.  Votes can shift towards a
4:119:7831:14:15:91:519:338:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:political party if its policies, related to migration, increase voters’ utility and if voters
4:120:7924:15:14:91:519:323:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:perceive immigration as an important issue.  The second channel, instead, is related
4:121:8008:14:15:91:519:309:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:to  the  direct  political  role  of  immigrants  as  voters.   As  they  become  naturalized,
4:122:8102:15:28:91:504:294:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:immigrants affect elections, to the extent that they vote differently from natives.
4:123:8185:28:15:109:520:266:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:As far as the first (indirect) effect of immigrants is concerned, voters can perceive
4:124:8270:15:14:91:519:251:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the local presence of immigrants as associated with local amenities or dis-amenities
4:125:8354:14:15:91:519:237:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:– such as cultural effects – or with changes in economic variables – such as wages,
4:126:8437:15:18:91:519:222:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:employment, taxes and public goods – that they care about and that parties’ poli-
4:127:8518:18:15:105:519:204:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:2For  both  natives  and  immigrants,  the  sample  includes  wage-earning,  civilian  employees,  age
4:128:8620:15:9:91:117:189:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:18-64.
4:129:8626:9:15:105:519:180:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:3Examples are Giuliano (2007), Alesina and Giuliano (2011) which show how immigrants affect
4:130:8717:15:12:91:519:165:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:the transmission of social norms.  Butcher and Piehl (1998), Chalfin (2015) and Spenkuch (2013)
4:131:8812:12:0:91:362:153:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:analyze the effect of immigration on crime rates in U.S. cities.
5:132:8877:0:15:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:cies can influence.  These policies may be directly related to migration, like migration
5:133:8965:15:14:91:519:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:policy, or may be other types of government interventions.  In the latter case, for ex-
5:134:9052:14:15:91:519:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:ample, if native voters think that immigrants generate a net fiscal transfer from them,
5:135:9139:15:14:91:519:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:they might be pushed to vote for the Republican party which favors less redistribu-
5:136:9222:14:15:91:520:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:tion and less safety-net policies.4As far as the second (direct) effect of immigrants is
5:137:9310:15:14:91:519:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:concerned, instead, once they are naturalized, immigrants will also cast their vote ex-
5:138:9397:14:15:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:pressing their electoral preferences, which are usually different from those of natives:
5:139:9485:15:14:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:This will affect the aggregate election outcome.  In the U.S.,  where naturalization
5:140:9569:14:15:91:520:569:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:rates are high5, this second channel is likely to be important.  Immigration, there-
5:141:9653:15:14:91:519:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:fore, may have different impacts depending on the balance of immigrant citizens and
5:142:9736:14:29:91:513:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:non-citizens and on how strong the voting response of citizens is to their presence.
5:143:9820:29:14:109:520:511:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:The U.S. press and media, as well as political analysts (e.g.  Gimpel (2014)), have
5:144:9903:14:15:91:519:497:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:for the most part focused on the direct effect (the second described above), pointing
5:145:9988:15:14:91:519:482:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:out the potential adverse impact that migrants can have on the electoral success of
5:146:10071:14:15:91:519:468:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the  Republican  party,  as  immigrants  seem  more  likely  to  vote  for  the  Democratic
5:147:10162:15:14:91:520:453:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Party.6Many political commentators even see an inevitable demise of the Republi-
5:148:10242:14:15:91:519:439:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:can party, in the long-run, as first- and second-generation immigrants become more
5:149:10324:15:14:91:519:424:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:numerous.  Our analysis confirms this prediction by showing that, on average, im-
5:150:10405:14:14:91:519:410:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:migration to the U.S. has a significant and negative impact on the Republican vote
5:151:10487:14:15:91:519:396:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:share.  In particular, we find this effect in the House elections but not in other types
5:152:10575:15:14:91:519:381:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of elections (Senate, Presidential and Gubernatorial).  However an important aspect
5:153:10658:14:15:91:519:367:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of the political effect of migration, which has received less attention, is that natives’
5:154:10747:15:14:91:519:352:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:votes, too, could be affected by the increase in the share of immigrants, as mentioned
5:155:10833:14:15:91:520:338:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:above.7Our empirical analysis shows that this is the case.  When we distinguish be-
5:156:10916:15:14:91:519:323:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:tween the effect of naturalized and non-naturalized immigrants we find a significant,
5:157:11001:14:15:91:519:309:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:negative and linear effect of those naturalized on the share of Republican votes in the
5:158:11088:15:14:91:519:294:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:House elections.  On the other hand, when the share of non-naturalized immigrants
5:159:11169:14:14:91:519:280:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:increases, there is a small negative or insignificant linear effect on the share of Re-
5:160:11256:14:15:91:519:266:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:publican votes but, if we allow for a non-linear (quadratic) effect, we actually find a
5:161:11343:15:14:91:519:251:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:positive impact for large levels of immigrants’ shares (above 0.132).  In other words,
5:162:11429:14:18:91:519:237:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:native  voters’  political  preferences  move  towards  the  Republican  party  because  of
5:163:11520:18:16:105:519:219:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:4At the same time, if immigrants have only limited access to the welfare state, as can be the
5:164:11613:16:12:91:519:203:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:case with illegal immigrants, native voters might vote for the party in favor of redistribution and
5:165:11712:12:8:91:476:191:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:safety-net policies, if they believe that immigration is negatively affecting their incomes.
5:166:11804:8:12:105:493:183:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:A:5In our data set (1994-2012), naturalized immigrants are about 40% of total immigrants.
5:167:11891:12:12:105:306:171:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:A:6See first quote at the beginning of the paper.
5:168:11938:12:0:105:317:159:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:A:7See second quote at the beginning of the paper.
6:169:11987:0:15:91:520:685:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f1:B:highimmigration of non-citizens.  This is interesting and plausible given that, when
6:170:12071:15:14:91:519:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:non-naturalized immigrants – many of whom are new immigrants and some undocu-
6:171:12148:14:15:91:519:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:mented – become a large share in a state, perceptions by voters become acute, making
6:172:12232:15:14:91:519:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:immigration a salient feature in the voting decision of natives.  Our estimates reveal
6:173:12318:14:15:91:519:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that in states characterized by a very high non-naturalized immigrant share of the
6:174:12400:15:14:91:519:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:population (6 states in 2012:  California, District of Columbia, Nevada, New Jersey,
6:175:12484:14:15:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:New York and Texas), the Republican vote share in House elections is positively and
6:176:12567:15:14:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:significantly affected by an increase in new (non-naturalized) immigrants.  However,
6:177:12651:14:15:91:519:569:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:when the share of non-naturalized immigrants in the population is less than 13.2%,
6:178:12733:15:14:91:519:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the impact of an increase in this share on Republican votes is null to negative.  In this
6:179:12822:14:14:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:case, the main effect of immigration is to add voters to the electorate, who tend to
6:180:12906:14:15:91:519:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:vote for the Democratic party.  Overall our results are consistent with the hypothesis
6:181:12992:15:14:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that  naturalized  immigrants  are  less  likely  to  vote  for  the  Republican  party  than
6:182:13085:14:15:91:519:497:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:native  voters,  and  that  native  voters’  political  preferences  are  shifted  towards  the
6:183:13180:15:14:91:519:482:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Republicans, but only in states where the presence of non-naturalized immigrants is
6:184:13263:14:15:91:519:468:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:high.  Also note that the average U.S. state is one in which the negative direct impact
6:185:13350:15:14:91:519:453:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:on Republican votes from naturalized immigrants prevails.  For example, in the year
6:186:13433:14:15:91:519:439:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:2012, the average share of non-citizen immigrants was 6.8% significantly below the
6:187:13515:15:28:91:206:424:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:13.2% threshold value.
6:188:13537:28:15:109:520:396:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:As  mentioned  above,  we  find  that  on  average  immigration  to  the  U.S.  has  a
6:189:13623:15:14:91:519:381:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:significant and negative impact on the Republican vote share. Yet, empirical evidence
6:190:13708:14:15:91:519:367:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:from some European countries is exactly the opposite as it shows that immigrant
6:191:13787:15:14:91:520:352:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:inflowsimprovethe electoral success of right-wing parties (see Barone et al. (2014)
6:192:13870:14:15:91:519:338:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:and Halla et al. (2012)).  Our results, differentiating between citizen and non-citizen
6:193:13957:15:14:91:519:323:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:migrants, suggest one possible explanation of the difference between the European
6:194:14038:14:15:91:519:309:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:and U.S. findings.  We find that the political effect of immigration crucially depends
6:195:14124:15:14:91:519:294:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:on the extent to which migrants can participate in the political process. To the extent
6:196:14211:14:14:91:519:280:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that in Europe naturalization rates and/or political participation of immigrants are
6:197:14295:14:15:91:519:266:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:low, the indirect political effect of migration working through migrants’ impact on
6:198:14378:15:14:91:519:251:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:existing  voters’  preferences  should  be  the  main  one  at  work.   In  the  U.S.,  where
6:199:14471:14:15:91:519:237:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:naturalization  rates  are  large,  the  direct  effect  of  immigrants  on  votes  is  sizable
6:200:14566:15:14:91:519:222:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:and dominates on average.  However, when we differentiate across states/years cells
6:201:14649:14:15:91:519:208:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:according  to  their  share  of  non-naturalized  migrants,  we  also  find  that  six  states
6:202:14743:15:14:91:519:193:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:have a high enough share of non-naturalized immigrants such that this group has a
6:203:14824:14:18:91:478:179:12:g_d0_f1:8:g_d0_f3:B:positive effect on Republican votes, consistent with the European findings.8
6:204:14900:18:16:105:519:161:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:8According to the American Community Survey (ACS), in 2008 the U.S. naturalization rate was
6:205:14991:16:0:91:519:145:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:43%.  In many European countries naturalization rates were lower in the same year, for example in
7:206:15089:0:14:109:520:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:Our analysis is both theoretical and empirical.  We first develop a simple model,
7:207:15170:14:15:91:519:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:which provides intuition about the main channels at work and which allows us to
7:208:15249:15:14:91:519:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:derive  theory-based  empirical  specifications.   Our  empirical  analysis  addresses  the
7:209:15340:14:15:91:519:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:key identification issue.  A least square estimate of the correlation between votes and
7:210:15427:15:14:91:519:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:immigration could be biased by spurious correlation due to the fact that immigrants
7:211:15510:14:15:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:self-select into geographical areas – and might go where natives are more favorable
7:212:15593:15:14:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:to their presence.  We use a novel set of instruments for our main explanatory vari-
7:213:15677:14:15:91:519:569:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:ables, which are the overall share of migrants and, respectively, the naturalized and
7:214:15762:15:14:91:519:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:non-naturalized shares in a state.  Shift-share instruments  ̈ı¿œ la Card (2001) – based
7:215:15850:14:14:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:on the size of past settlement of immigrants from a given country of origin across
7:216:15932:14:15:91:519:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:U.S.  states  –  have  been  widely  used  in  the  literature,  based  on  the  idea  that  one
7:217:16028:15:14:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:important determinant of migration is family and friends networks (Munshi (2003)).
7:218:16110:14:15:91:519:497:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:However, one concern that has been raised is that the past location of immigrants
7:219:16191:15:14:91:519:482:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:across destinations might be correlated with past local economic and political con-
7:220:16274:14:15:91:519:468:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:ditions.  To the extent that these conditions are persistent and hence correlated over
7:221:16360:15:14:91:519:453:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:time, this would invalidate the exclusion restriction of shift-share instruments  ̈ı¿œ la
7:222:16449:14:15:91:519:439:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Card (2001).  We address this concern.  The unifying theme of our novel instruments
7:223:16532:15:14:91:519:424:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:is that the distance between a country of origin of immigrants and a U.S. state is
7:224:16614:14:14:91:519:410:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:likely to be an exogenous determinant of the size of settlements of immigrants from
7:225:16697:14:15:91:519:396:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that source and, likely, not correlated with other factors affecting the political cli-
7:226:16784:15:14:91:519:381:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:mate in the state.  To construct the instrument for the overall share of immigrants in
7:227:16870:14:15:91:519:367:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:a U.S. state, we use a shift-share IV, where predicted migration shares are inversely
7:228:16955:15:14:91:519:352:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:proportional to the state’s distance from the country of origin. Similarly, to construct
7:229:17043:14:15:91:519:338:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the instrument for the naturalized migrant share, we use data on aggregate yearly
7:230:17124:15:14:91:519:323:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:inflows of naturalized immigrants from a given country of origin and apportion these
7:231:17208:14:15:91:519:309:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:data across states according to shares that are inversely proportional to the distance
7:232:17294:15:14:91:519:294:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:measure.  For the non-naturalized migrant share – which includes, especially in years
7:233:17379:14:14:91:519:280:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:after 1990, illegal migrants – we combine data on national-level yearly border appre-
7:234:17464:14:15:91:519:266:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:hensions, that provide a proxy for total undocumented immigration in a year, with
7:235:17545:15:14:91:519:251:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:information on distance of each U.S. state from the U.S.–Mexico border.  One can ar-
7:236:17629:14:15:91:519:237:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:gue that the instrument for non-naturalized immigrants mainly captures the changes
7:237:17711:15:14:91:519:222:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:in the group of undocumented Mexicans and Central Americans.  We think of this
7:238:17789:14:15:91:519:208:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:point as a strength of our identification.  First,  this is a very large and significant
7:239:17877:15:21:91:519:193:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:group among the non-naturalized immigrants.  Second, this is the group that likely
7:240:17959:21:12:91:519:172:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:Italy (14%) and in Austria (34%) (Reichel (2012)).  The analysis of the difference in the political
7:241:18058:12:12:91:519:160:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:impact of migration in the U.S. vs.  Europe is beyond the scope of this paper and is the focus of
7:242:18155:12:0:91:180:148:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:Mayda et al. (2015).
8:243:18176:0:15:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:encourages the strongest political response of citizens in terms of their vote.  After
8:244:18262:15:14:91:519:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:all,  it  is  by  leveraging  the  discomfort  of  citizens  at  the  presence  of  large  numbers
8:245:18360:14:15:91:519:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of undocumented immigrants that several Republican candidates try to rally their
8:246:18440:15:29:91:116:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:base.
8:247:18445:29:14:109:520:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:The outline of the paper is as follows.  Section 2 surveys the existing literature
8:248:18527:14:15:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:related to this paper.  In Section 3, we develop a theoretical model that characterizes
8:249:18614:15:14:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the indirect effect of new migrants (through changes in existing voters’ voting behav-
8:250:18700:14:15:91:519:569:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:ior) separately from their direct effect (through the inclusion of naturalized migrants
8:251:18787:15:14:91:519:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:as new voters).  We then describe the data and how we construct the key variables in
8:252:18871:14:14:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Section 4.  In Section 5 we present, respectively, a naive and a model-based empirical
8:253:18957:14:15:91:519:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:specification that we use for estimation.  We also discuss identification and present
8:254:19042:15:14:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the main empirical results.  In section 6 we calculate the effect of different policies on
8:255:19132:14:15:91:519:497:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the vote share of the Republican party as predicted by our estimates.  We also use
8:256:19214:15:14:91:519:482:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:data on immigration and voting behavior in some representative U.S. states in 2008
8:257:19296:14:15:91:519:468:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:and 2012 to illustrate the relevance and plausibility of the estimated effects.  In Sec-
8:258:19384:15:14:91:519:453:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:tion 7, we investigate potential channels through which non naturalized immigrants
8:259:19466:14:40:91:467:439:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:affect the voting behavior of existing voters.  Finally, Section 8 concludes.
8:260:19543:40:26:91:277:399:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:2    Related Literature
8:261:19566:26:15:91:519:373:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Our analysis is related to the theoretical and empirical contributions in the economics
8:262:19653:15:29:91:439:358:12:g_d0_f1:8:g_d0_f3:B:literature that analyze the effect of immigrants on voting behavior.9
8:263:19722:29:14:109:520:329:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:A large part of the theoretical economic literature has focused on voting behavior
8:264:19804:14:15:91:519:315:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:on immigration policy as a function of the skill composition of immigrants and na-
8:265:19886:15:14:91:519:300:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:tives.  The seminal paper in this literature is Benhabib (1996), which derives the skill
8:266:19974:14:14:91:519:286:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:composition requirements that would be imposed on potential immigrants, under ma-
8:267:20055:14:15:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:jority voting, assuming that the only effect of migration is through the labor market.
8:268:20141:15:14:91:519:257:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Ortega (2005) analyzes the trade-off arising in a dynamic version of Benhabib (1996)
8:269:20225:14:15:91:519:243:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:model in which immigrants gain the right to vote and, therefore, affect the political
8:270:20310:15:14:91:519:228:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:balance of the destination country.  The arrival in the destination country of immi-
8:271:20394:14:15:91:519:214:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:grants,  whose skill composition depends on the existing immigration policy,  alters
8:272:20478:15:17:91:519:199:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the skilled-to-unskilled labor ratio of the work force in the destination country.  This,
8:273:20567:17:16:105:519:182:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:9While our work is related to contributions in the political science literature on the same topic, for
8:274:20669:16:12:91:519:166:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:the sake of space our survey focuses on economics papers.  Importantly, though, to our knowledge,
8:275:20766:12:0:91:474:154:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:no works in the political science literature carry out the same type of analysis as we do.
9:276:20857:0:15:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:in turn, affects the current-period skill premium as well as the skill composition of
9:277:20942:15:14:91:519:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:next period’s electorate, and thus the political balance and migration policies in the
9:278:21028:14:15:91:519:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:future.   On  the  one  hand,  skilled  (unskilled)  natives  prefer  an  immigration  policy
9:279:21121:15:14:91:519:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that  admits  unskilled  (skilled)  immigrants  to  their  country  because  of  their  wage
9:280:21213:14:15:91:519:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:effects.  On the other hand, the arrival of unskilled (skilled) immigrants potentially
9:281:21299:15:14:91:519:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:shifts the political equilibrium by increasing the number of unskilled (skilled) voters
9:282:21386:14:15:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:in the next period.  These two opposite effects could produce a cycle equilibrium in
9:283:21470:15:14:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:which the political majority switches from one group to the other.  Alternatively, a
9:284:21554:14:15:91:519:569:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:quota equilibrium could prevail in which the group in the majority – either skilled or
9:285:21640:15:14:91:519:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:unskilled – admits immigrants of the opposite type but limits their number through
9:286:21722:14:14:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:quotas, in order to retain future political power.  Finally, Razin et al. (2011) focus on
9:287:21811:14:15:91:519:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the joint decision of voters on immigration and redistribution policies, respectively.
9:288:21897:15:14:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:They emphasize how, in terms of immigration and redistribution, a democratic state
9:289:21979:14:15:91:519:497:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:would produce policies that are consistent with each other so that, when immigration
9:290:22063:15:14:91:519:482:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:is more open, natives restrict redistribution for fear of net transfers to immigrants,
9:291:22149:14:15:91:519:468:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:while when immigration is more restricted, they are willing to allow more redistri-
9:292:22232:15:14:91:519:453:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:bution.  The theoretical models provide predictions on how natives of different skills
9:293:22318:14:15:91:519:439:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:prefer more or less immigrants,  also as a function of the amount of redistribution
9:294:22401:15:28:91:204:424:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:provided by the state.
9:295:22423:28:15:109:520:396:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:The existing empirical literature for the U.S. provides indirect evidence for the
9:296:22504:15:14:91:519:381:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:effect of immigrants on voting behavior, mainly by analyzing what determines the
9:297:22584:14:15:91:519:367:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:preferences of U.S. individuals about immigrants. For example, Scheve and Slaughter
9:298:22667:15:14:91:519:352:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:(2001)  analyze  the  labor-market  drivers  of  individual  preferences  on  immigration
9:299:22756:14:15:91:519:338:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:policy  –  using  the  1992  NES  survey  –  and  find  that  more-skilled  respondents  are
9:300:22848:15:14:91:520:323:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:significantly  less  likely  to  be  anti-immigration.10Hanson  et  al.  (2007)  extend  the
9:301:22940:14:15:91:519:309:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:previous analysis by accounting for the impact of public-finance considerations on
9:302:23022:15:14:91:519:294:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:U.S. migration attitudes.  This paper shows that the negative impact of individual
9:303:23104:14:14:91:519:280:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:skill on anti-migration preferences is weaker in states characterized by high exposure
9:304:23190:14:15:91:520:266:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:to immigrant fiscal pressures.11Looking at similar surveys for European countries,
9:305:23272:15:14:91:519:251:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Card et al. (2012) show that while the perception of economic gains from immigrants
9:306:23355:14:18:91:519:237:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:vary across skills of natives, it is the perception of the impact of immigrants on local
9:307:23443:18:16:101:519:219:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:10Given that in the U.S. immigrants are on average less skilled than natives, respondents’ percep-
9:308:23541:16:12:91:519:203:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:tions are in line with the predictions of the multi-cone HO model (without factor-price insensitivity)
9:309:23643:12:8:91:287:191:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:and of the factor-proportions-analysis model.
9:310:23688:8:16:101:519:183:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:11For  papers  analyzing  the  labor-market  and  welfare-state  determinants  of  public  opinion  on
9:311:23790:16:12:91:519:167:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:migration across countries, see for example Mayda (2006), Facchini and Mayda (2009) and O’rourke
9:312:23886:12:0:91:180:155:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:and Sinnott (2006)).
10:313:23907:0:15:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:communities, culture and amenities that drives the policy preference of natives on
10:314:23989:15:29:91:374:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:immigration (stricter or looser immigration policies).12.
10:315:24046:29:14:109:520:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:More  directly  related  to  our  work  are  some  papers  that  analyze,  for  different
10:316:24135:14:15:91:519:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:European countries, how the inflow of immigrants impacts the electoral success of
10:317:24216:15:14:91:519:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:right-wing parties. In particular, Barone et al. (2014) empirically analyze the effect of
10:318:24305:14:15:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:immigration to Italy on political outcomes in the 2001, 2006 and 2008 national elec-
10:319:24389:15:14:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:tions.  This paper finds that the inflows of immigrants into a municipality increased
10:320:24474:14:15:91:519:569:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the share of votes going to the centre-right party, which was more conservative on
10:321:24556:15:14:91:519:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:immigration issues than the centre-left one.  Similarly, Halla et al. (2012) estimate
10:322:24641:14:14:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the impact of immigrant inflows in Austria on the share of votes for a far-right-wing
10:323:24726:14:15:91:519:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:party  (the  Freedom  Party  of  Austria).   They  find  evidence  of  a  positive  and  sig-
10:324:24819:15:14:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:nificant  effect  at  the  neighborhood  level.   Both  papers  use  shift-share  instruments
10:325:24912:14:15:90:520:497:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B: ̈ı¿œ la Card (2001).  Finally, Otto and Steinhardt (2014) analyze the impact of the
10:326:24996:15:14:91:519:482:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:share of foreign citizens on election outcomes, using variation over time across city
10:327:25081:14:15:91:519:468:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:districts in Hamburg between 1987 and 2000.  The authors find evidence of a positive
10:328:25165:15:14:91:519:453:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:correlation between the district’s immigrant share and the share of votes for extreme
10:329:25250:14:15:91:519:439:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:right-wing parties – with a clearly anti-immigration stand – and of a negative cor-
10:330:25333:15:14:91:519:424:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:relation between the district’s immigrant share and the share of votes for the Green
10:331:25417:14:14:91:519:410:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Party – which had a pro-migration position.  The authors give a causal interpretation
10:332:25502:14:15:91:519:396:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:to these results based on a fixed-effects empirical strategy and additional robustness
10:333:25588:15:14:91:519:381:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:checks,  which  account  for  the  endogeneity  of  the  location  decision  of  natives  and
10:334:25681:14:29:91:389:367:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:immigrants.  They do not instrument the immigrant flows.
10:335:25737:29:15:109:520:338:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:Relative to these papers,  our paper is the first to analyze separately the effect
10:336:25819:15:14:91:519:323:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of naturalized and non naturalized immigrants.  It is also the first to focus on U.S.
10:337:25904:14:15:91:519:309:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:elections, using variation across U.S. states instrumented with a distance-based proxy
10:338:25990:15:39:91:298:294:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:for immigration from different countries.
10:339:26031:39:27:91:274:255:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:3    Theoretical model
10:340:26053:27:14:91:519:228:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:In  this  section  we  present  a  simple  model  that  allows  us  to  investigate  the  direct
10:341:26149:14:15:91:519:214:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:and indirect effects of immigrants on parties’ voting shares.  Each of the two effects
10:342:26235:15:17:91:519:199:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:depends on a well identified group of immigrants.  The direct effect of immigrants is
10:343:26320:17:16:101:519:182:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:12A related line of research looks at how U.S. politicians vote on topics related to immigration
10:344:26416:16:12:91:519:166:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:policies, as a function of characteristics of their districts.  Interesting examples of this literature are
10:345:26523:12:0:91:344:154:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:Conconi et al. (2012) and Facchini and Steinhardt (2011).
11:346:26581:0:15:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:due to the inclusion of new voters, i.e.  citizen migrants13, who may have a different
11:347:26667:15:14:91:519:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:voting behavior than natives but, for several demographic characteristics, are similar
11:348:26753:14:15:91:519:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:to natives.  Hence a change in the fraction of voting immigrants in the electorate may
11:349:26839:15:14:91:519:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:affect the share of Republican votes because of their different political preferences.
11:350:26925:14:15:91:519:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Non-voting immigrants (who are not citizens, and often temporary or undocumented)
11:351:27006:15:14:91:519:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:do  not  affect  election  outcomes  through  this  channel.   The  second  channel  is  the
11:352:27098:14:15:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:indirect effect of new immigrants who are not citizens at first on the vote of citizens.
11:353:27186:15:14:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:The arrival of new (non-citizen) immigrants may induce voters to respond by altering
11:354:27270:14:15:91:519:569:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:their party preference in the polls in response to what they perceive as a threat or
11:355:27354:15:28:91:170:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:an opportunity.
11:356:27369:28:15:109:520:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:To formalize this point, we present a very simple theoretical model that delivers

15:584:38545:17:0:346:359:393:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:?:Vit
15:585:38548:0:26:370:520:402:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:+βxXit+εit(8)
15:586:38561:26:15:109:519:376:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:In this specification, we are assuming a linear effect,β1, of new non-citizen im-
15:587:38642:15:14:91:519:361:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:migrants  on  the  share  of  Republican  votes.   However,  as  mentioned  above,  it  is
15:588:38732:14:14:91:519:347:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:important to allow for the non-linearity that captures the increased salience of im-
15:589:38816:14:15:91:519:333:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:migration in elections, as the share of new immigrants increase.  We can do this in
15:590:38899:15:47:91:312:318:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the following linear-quadratic specification:
15:591:38944:47:0:114:200:271:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:?:rit=si+qt+βL
15:592:38956:0:16:207:246:279:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:?:NCMit
15:593:38961:16:0:202:252:263:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:?:Mit+Nit
15:594:38968:0:0:256:281:271:12:g_d0_f1:8:g_d0_f8:?:+βQ
15:595:38971:0:9:283:292:288:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:?:(
15:596:38972:9:16:299:338:279:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:?:NCMit
15:597:38977:16:0:293:343:263:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:?:Mit+Nit
15:598:38984:0:17:345:358:288:12:g_d0_f9:8:g_d0_f3:?:)2
15:599:38986:17:0:361:384:271:12:g_d0_f1:8:g_d0_f3:?:+β2
15:600:38989:0:16:386:412:279:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:?:CMit
15:601:38993:16:0:392:405:263:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:?:Vit
15:602:38996:0:33:416:520:271:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:+βxXit+εit(9)
15:603:39009:33:29:109:488:238:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:Equations (8) and (9) above are the basis for our main empirical analysis.
15:604:39083:29:14:109:520:209:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:Finally note that the perceived effect of Republicans on voters’ income can work
15:605:39163:14:15:91:519:195:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:through several channels.  For example, new immigrants can be thought of, by voters,
15:606:39247:15:14:91:519:180:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:as the cause of favorable or adverse labor-market effects.  According to theory, the
15:607:39331:14:15:91:519:166:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:latter  ones  depend  on  the  skill  composition  of  non-citizen  immigrants  relative  to
15:608:39423:15:0:91:519:151:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:voters and on how skilled voters are.  New immigrants are also likely to be associated
16:609:39511:0:15:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:with changes in the welfare state, which can be favorable or adverse depending on
16:610:39592:15:14:91:519:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:how  rich  non-citizen  migrants  are  relative  to  voters.   In  particular,  if  non-citizen
16:611:39687:14:15:91:519:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:migrants are poorer than voters, they are likely to be a fiscal burden.  The opposite
16:612:39772:15:14:91:519:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:is true if they are richer than voters. The welfare-state impact of non-citizen migrants
16:613:39860:14:15:91:519:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:will also imply income distribution effects which depend on the type of adjustment of
16:614:39945:15:14:91:519:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the welfare state to migration (see Facchini and Mayda (2009)) and how rich voters
16:615:40027:14:15:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:are.   Finally,  the  perceived  effect  of  Republicans  on  voters’  non-pecuniary  utility
16:616:40120:15:14:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:can be linked to the cultural effects of new (non-citizen) migrants, which are likely
16:617:40205:14:15:91:519:569:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:to  depend  on  how  different  voters  and  migrants  are  in  terms  of  language  spoken,
16:618:40297:15:14:91:519:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:religion, historical and institutional background.  We will account for these channels
16:619:40383:14:14:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:through which the non-citizen migrant share affects Republican votes in Section 7
16:620:40464:14:40:91:124:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:below.
16:621:40470:40:27:91:314:486:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:4    Data and key variables
16:622:40497:27:14:91:520:459:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:As suggested by the model above, to analyze the electoral outcome of stateiin year
16:623:40579:14:15:91:520:445:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f1:B:t, we need to analyze three groups of individuals.  First is the group of natives (whose
16:624:40667:15:14:91:520:430:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:number is equal toNit) who constitute in all states the majority of voters.  Second
16:625:40750:14:14:91:519:416:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:is  the  group  of  citizen  immigrants  who  can  vote  and  may  have  different  electoral
16:626:40843:14:15:91:519:402:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:preference from natives.  Finally is the group of non-citizen immigrants who cannot
16:627:40926:15:14:91:519:387:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:vote but whose presence may affect the vote of citizens.  Thus immigrants or foreign-
16:628:41011:14:15:91:519:373:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:born,  whose  total  number  in  stateiand  yeartisMit,  are  divided  into  citizens,
16:629:41097:15:14:91:520:358:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:whose number is equal toCMitand non-citizens, whose number isNCMit,so that
16:630:41171:14:15:91:520:344:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f1:B:Mit=NCMit+CMit.   We  obtain  data  on  natives,  immigrant  citizens  and  non-
16:631:41251:15:14:91:519:329:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:citizens from the Current Population Survey (CPS). The sample period consists of
16:632:41331:14:15:91:519:315:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the years between 1994 and 2012.  We aggregate the individual-level data to the state
16:633:41416:15:14:91:519:300:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:level using the CPS sampling weights.  We estimate our model at the state level since
16:634:41501:14:14:91:519:286:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the CPS data set is not representative at a lower level of geographical disaggregation
16:635:41587:14:15:91:520:272:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:such as county or electoral district16.  However, recognizing that it is important to
16:636:41672:15:14:91:519:257:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:provide results at a finer level of geographical disaggregation, we assume in Section
16:637:41757:14:15:91:519:243:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:5 below that the effect of different groups of immigrants on the share of Republican
16:638:41841:15:14:91:519:228:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:votes,  estimated  at  the  state-level,  holds  at  the  Congressional  district  level.   This
16:639:41937:14:15:91:519:214:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:way we can provide the magnitude of the simulated effects of immigrants on votes
16:640:42017:15:17:91:222:199:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:at this level of geography.
16:641:42044:17:16:101:519:182:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:16Alternative data sets we could have used are the Census data – but these data are only every
16:642:42138:16:12:91:519:166:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:ten years – or the American Community Survey (ACS) data – but these data are only available
16:643:42229:12:12:91:519:154:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:from 2000 on and are yearly representative at low geographical level (such as county) only from
16:644:42324:12:0:91:114:142:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:2005.
17:645:42331:0:14:109:520:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:We callmshitthe immigrant share of the (working-age labor-force) population
17:646:42406:14:32:91:229:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:which is defined as follows:
17:647:42434:32:0:258:299:624:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f1:?:mshit=
17:648:42440:0:16:319:336:632:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:Mit
17:649:42443:16:0:304:351:616:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:?:Mit+Nit
17:650:42450:0:27:499:520:624:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:(10)
17:651:42454:27:14:109:520:597:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:It  captures  the  number  of  foreign-born  individuals  (both  males  and  females),
17:652:42540:14:14:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:aged  18-64,  as  a  share  of  the  total  labor-force  population  of  that  state  (aged  18-
17:653:42636:14:15:91:520:569:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:64).17This is a measure of the overall presence of foreign-born individuals in state
17:654:42720:15:14:91:520:554:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f1:B:i’s population in yeart.  We also define the immigrant citizen and non-citizen shares
17:655:42805:14:15:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of the population,cmshitandncmshit,  which are equal toCMit/(Mit+Nit) and
17:656:42878:15:14:91:520:525:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f1:B:NCMit/(Mit+Nit), respectively.  The sum of the immigrant citizen and non-citizen
17:657:42958:14:15:91:520:511:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:shares equalsmshit.  To investigate more directly the channel through which citizen
17:658:43041:15:14:91:519:496:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:immigrants as new voters affect the electoral vote, we also define the citizen migrants
17:659:43128:14:15:91:520:482:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f1:B:votingshare,cmvoteshit=CMit/Vit, which is the share of citizen migrants in the
17:660:43206:15:14:91:519:467:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:voting populationVit= (Nit+CMit).  According to the theoretical model, it is the
17:661:43286:14:14:91:519:453:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:citizen migrantsvotingshare which has an impact on Republican votes proportional
17:662:43366:14:15:91:519:439:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:to the difference in average propensity to vote Republican of native and immigrant
17:663:43448:15:14:91:519:424:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:citizens.   Finally,  the  voting  population  is  related  to  the  total  population  by  the
17:664:43543:14:29:91:196:410:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:following expression:
17:665:43564:29:21:241:370:381:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:?:Mit+Nit=Vit+NCMit
17:666:43581:21:15:109:520:360:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:i.e.,  the  total  population  is  equal  to  the  number  of  voters  plus  the  number  of
17:667:43673:15:28:91:212:345:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:non-citizen immigrants.
17:668:43696:28:15:109:520:317:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:The  election  data  are  from  the  Congressional  Quarterly  data  set  and  include
17:669:43782:15:14:91:519:302:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:presidential, congressional (House and Senate) and gubernatorial elections from 1994
17:670:43866:14:15:91:519:288:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:to  the  present.   Our  main  outcome  variable  is  the  share  of  votes  that  goes  to  the
17:671:43962:15:32:91:332:273:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:candidate affiliated with the Republican Party:
17:672:44009:32:0:241:265:241:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f1:?:rit=

17:676:44040:25:15:109:520:216:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f1:A:Republican V otesitrepresents the number of people that voted for the Republican
17:677:44120:15:18:91:418:201:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:party, whereasAVitis the number of votes in stateiand yeart.

18:679:44249:0:23:91:263:685:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.1    Summary statistics
18:680:44274:23:14:91:519:662:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:After matching the election data with the CPS data at the state-year level, the final
18:681:44359:14:15:91:519:648:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:sample contains 1306 state-year observations across four types of elections.  Table 1
18:682:44444:15:14:91:519:633:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:contains the summary statistics of the election and population data, including the
18:683:44526:14:14:91:519:619:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:control variables which will be used in the empirical analysis. The election data shows
18:684:44613:14:15:91:519:605:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that, across all elections and years over the period 1994-2012, the average Republican
18:685:44699:15:14:91:519:590:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:vote  share  was  49.0  percent,  while  the  Democratic  vote  share  was  lower,  at  46.9
18:686:44791:14:15:91:519:576:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:percent.   The  remaining,  small,  share  of  votes  accrued  to  third  party  candidates.
18:687:44883:15:14:91:519:561:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Figure 1 in the appendix shows a map of all U.S. states, with darker color for states
18:688:44968:14:15:91:519:547:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:with larger average Republican vote share pooling all years and elections between
18:689:45049:15:14:91:519:532:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:1994 and 2012.  The Republican vote share has been higher in states of the South
18:690:45129:14:15:91:519:518:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:and in the central United States while it has been relatively low in States of the West
18:691:45216:15:28:91:232:503:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Coast and of New England.
18:692:45241:28:15:109:520:475:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:Figure 2 plots the corresponding spatial distribution of immigrants in the years
18:693:45321:15:14:91:519:460:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:1994  and  2012.   California  had  the  highest  share  of  immigrants  in  both  years:  28
18:694:45414:14:15:91:519:446:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:percent in the year 1994 and 35.4 percent in 2012.  New England states, as well as
18:695:45496:15:14:91:519:431:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:some southern states such as Texas, Arizona and Florida also had high shares.  The
18:696:45578:14:15:91:519:417:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:states with the lowest immigration share are Kentucky in 1994 (0.4 percent) and West
18:697:45662:15:14:91:519:402:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Virginia in 2012 (1.3 percent).  Overall, the share of immigrants steadily increased
18:698:45746:14:15:91:519:388:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:over time.  The nation-wide average share of immigrants in the total population was
18:699:45829:15:28:91:434:373:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:9.1 percent in year 1994 and it rose to 17 percent in the year 2012.
18:700:45897:28:15:109:520:345:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:The overall share of immigrants in the population combines the two groups that
18:701:45975:15:14:91:519:330:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:we  want  to  consider  separately.   We  see  from  Table  1  that  about  39  percent  of
18:702:46066:14:15:91:519:316:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:immigrants are citizens and the remaining 61 percent are non-citizens.  The share of
18:703:46150:15:14:91:519:301:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:citizens has increased over time as the number of naturalized citizens increased by
18:704:46233:14:15:91:519:287:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:more than the number of new immigrants.  Over the past decade,  while the share
18:705:46312:15:14:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of non-citizen immigrants in the U.S. population increased from 6.3 percent in 1994
18:706:46395:14:15:91:519:258:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:to  9.5  percent  in  2012,  the  share  of  citizen  immigrants  went  from  2.8  percent  in
18:707:46489:15:14:91:519:243:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:1994 to 7.4 percent in 2012.  As more and more citizens become naturalized, their
18:708:46570:14:14:91:519:229:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:importance in the voting population increases as well. In year 1994, the average share
18:709:46656:14:15:91:519:215:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:was 3 percent and climbed to 8.2 percent in the year 2012.  The share of immigrants
18:710:46739:15:14:91:519:200:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that are eligible to vote varies greatly across states.  Kentucky has the lowest share of
18:711:46828:14:15:91:519:186:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:0.1 percent in 1994 and California the highest with 20.3 percent in 2012.  Moreover
18:712:46911:15:14:91:519:171:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:there  is  a  strong  correlation  between  the  share  of  non-citizen  immigrants  and  the
18:713:47004:14:15:91:519:157:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:share of citizen immigrants across states.  Those states with large presence of citizen
18:714:47091:15:0:91:519:142:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:immigrants as a share of the voting population also had large presence of non-citizen
19:715:47178:0:15:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:immigrants as a share of the population.  While one may think that this correlation
19:716:47261:15:14:91:519:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:makes it hard to separately identify the impact of each of these two groups on voting
19:717:47346:14:15:91:519:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:outcomes,  the  correlation  in  the changes  of  these  variables,  which  is  the  variation
19:718:47440:15:29:91:316:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:used to identify the effects, is much smaller.
19:719:47486:29:14:109:520:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:In terms of the control variables that we include in the voting equation, we follow
19:720:47569:14:15:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the  existing  literature,  especially  Della  Vigna  and  Kaplan  (2007)  and  include  the
19:721:47661:15:14:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:share of the voting population in each education group (high school dropouts, high
19:722:47743:14:15:91:519:569:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:school graduates, some college, college graduates and more than college), the share
19:723:47826:15:14:91:519:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of African Americans and Hispanics, the unemployment rate, the share of the state
19:724:47907:14:14:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that is urban as well as the share of males, the marriage rate and the income level
19:725:47990:14:40:91:191:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:(shown in Table 1).
19:726:48009:40:30:91:279:486:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:5    Empirical Analysis
19:727:48032:30:22:91:273:456:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:5.1    The naive regression
19:728:48059:22:15:91:519:434:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Before analyzing the causal relation between different types of immigrants and elec-
19:729:48143:15:14:91:519:419:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:toral outcomes, we show here some simple correlations. Considering total immigrants
19:730:48226:14:15:91:519:405:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:as a share of the adult population, we analyze whether one detects a correlation in
19:731:48309:15:14:91:519:390:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the data between this variable and the share of votes to the Republican Party.  As
19:732:48391:14:15:91:519:376:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:preliminary evidence, in Figure 3 we show the scatterplot of the change between 1994
19:733:48475:15:14:91:519:361:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:and 2012 in the fraction of Republican votes in the House of Representatives and the
19:734:48559:14:14:91:519:347:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:change in the same period in total immigrants as a share of the adult population,
19:735:48640:14:15:91:519:333:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:across  states.   The  visual  impression  is  clear  and  confirmed  by  the  statistical  sig-
19:736:48736:15:14:91:520:318:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:nificance of a regression line:  there is a significantnegativecorrelation between the
19:737:48822:14:15:91:519:304:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:growth in the immigrant share of the population and the Republican vote share in the
19:738:48906:15:14:91:519:289:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:House.  In the scatterplot we focus on House elections since these are the elections for
19:739:48994:14:15:91:519:275:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:which we find significant effects throughout the paper.  Moreover immigration policy
19:740:49078:15:14:91:519:260:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:is a federal issue and most of the important legislation on it has to be passed by the
19:741:49164:14:15:91:519:246:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:House of Representatives.  A more systematic way to show the negative correlation
19:742:49245:15:14:91:519:231:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:between the overall share of immigrants and the fraction of Republican votes is to
19:743:49327:14:14:91:519:217:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:pool all types of elections (Presidential (PE), Senate (SE), House of representatives
19:744:49412:14:29:91:459:203:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:(HE) and Gubernatorial (GE)) and estimate the following specification:
19:745:49482:29:21:196:520:174:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f1:A:rite=si+re+qt+βMmshit+βxXit+εite(12)
19:746:49518:21:0:109:520:153:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:where the dependent variableriteis the number of votes for the Republican party,
20:747:49600:0:15:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f7:B:out of the total number of votes, in statei(50 states), yeart(10 years) and electione
20:748:49685:15:14:91:520:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:(4 types of elections);mshit=Mit/(Mit+Nit) is the share of foreign-born individuals
20:749:49768:14:15:91:520:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:in stateiand yeart.18Controls include a vector of state fixed effectssi;  a vector
20:750:49850:15:14:91:520:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of  election-type  fixed  effectsre,  and  a  vector  of  year  fixed  effectsqt.   These  fixed
20:751:49946:14:15:91:519:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:effects control for systematic differences in election outcomes across states, election
20:752:50033:15:14:91:519:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:types  and  years  which  capture,  respectively,  persistent  political  differences  across
20:753:50126:14:15:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:states and year-specific or election-specific national tendencies.  We also control for
20:754:50213:15:14:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:variables which affect election outcomes according to the existing literature (see, for
20:755:50300:14:15:91:520:569:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:example, Della Vigna and Kaplan (2007)).  In particular,Xitis a vector of control
20:756:50381:15:14:91:520:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:variables for stateiin yeartwhich includes the share in the voting population of each
20:757:50466:14:14:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:education group (high school drop-outs, high school graduates, some college, college
20:758:50550:14:15:91:519:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:graduates, more than college), of African-Americans and Hispanics, of those living
20:759:50632:15:14:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:in urban areas, males, married individuals, the share of unemployed and, finally, the
20:760:50717:14:15:91:519:497:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:average income.  Note that we define all the control variables over the population of
20:761:50802:15:14:91:519:482:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:(potential) voters in each state and year, i.e.  natives plus citizen immigrants (aged
20:762:50888:14:15:91:519:468:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:18-64, in the civilian labor force).  We also estimate a regression separately for each
20:763:50975:15:14:91:519:453:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:election type, where we include the same vector of control variables as well as year
20:764:51059:14:29:91:204:439:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:and time fixed effects.
20:765:51082:29:14:109:520:410:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:First, we estimate equation (12) with ordinary least-squares, which establishes the
20:766:51165:14:15:91:519:396:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:correlation between the immigrant share and the Republican vote share controlling
20:767:51246:15:14:91:519:381:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:for an array of confounding factors.  Next, we push our “naive” regressions one step
20:768:51330:14:15:91:519:367:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:further  and  instrument  the  share  of  immigrants,  to  avoid  that  unobserved  time-
20:769:51419:15:14:91:519:352:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:varying  state  characteristics  might  attract  immigrants  and  at  the  same  time  shift
20:770:51511:14:15:91:519:338:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:votes away from (or in favor of) the Republican party.  The instrumental-variable
20:771:51592:15:14:91:519:323:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:methodology we use is based on Card (2001) but, importantly, differs from it as we
20:772:51674:14:15:91:519:309:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:replace the past distribution of immigrants from a given origin country to a given
20:773:51756:15:14:91:519:294:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:state with the inverse measure of distance between the origin and the state.  More
20:774:51838:14:14:91:520:280:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:precisely, letMotbe the number of immigrants from source countryowho live in the
20:775:51918:14:15:91:520:266:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:U.S. in yeartand letNtbe the total number of natives in the U.S. in yeart19.  We
20:776:51998:15:19:91:480:251:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:then construct our shift-share instrument, that we call (mshit)IVas follows:
20:777:52074:19:15:101:519:232:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:18Note that the total number of votes includes those to parties other than the Republican and
20:778:52167:15:9:91:176:217:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:Democratic parties.
