21:819:53825:28:17:109:520:204:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:Note that we aggregate the countries of origin of immigrants into 20 origin-country
21:820:53908:17:16:101:519:187:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:20To calculate the bilateral distances,  we follow Mayer and Zignago (2011),  i.e.  we define the
21:821:54005:16:12:91:519:171:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:distance in kilometers and calculate it by the Great Circle Distance formula. We use 32.19 kilometers
21:822:54106:12:12:91:519:159:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:as  inner-city  distance.   All  data  on  latitudes  and  longitudes  are  from  the  Global  Administrative
21:823:54215:12:0:91:318:147:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:Areas (GADM) database, see Hijmans et al. (2010).
22:824:54266:0:15:91:520:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:groups (such as Western Europe or Eastern Africa), thus the indexoinλoivaries
22:825:54343:15:29:91:254:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:across these 20 different groups.
22:826:54376:29:14:109:520:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:Importantly,  the  state  by  year  variation  of  the  instrument  is  only  driven  by
22:827:54464:14:15:91:519:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:national-level trends in the number of migrants from each origin – some origins ex-
22:828:54547:15:14:91:519:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:perienced large increases in migration to the U.S. (Central Americans, Chinese/East
22:829:54630:14:15:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Asians, Indians/Southwest Asians) while others experienced large declines (Western
22:830:54712:15:14:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:and Southern Europeans, Central Eastern Europeans) relative to earlier years – and
22:831:54794:14:15:91:519:569:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:by  the  geographic  location  of  U.S.  states  relative  to  the  countries  of  origin.   The
22:832:54890:15:14:91:519:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:time-varying aggregate migration trends and the geographic location of a state are
22:833:54972:14:14:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:likely to be uncorrelated with the changes in political climate and preferences in the
22:834:55058:14:15:91:519:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:state.  If the instrument affects the share of migrants in a state over time, we assume
22:835:55145:15:29:91:478:511:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that this is the channel through which it affects political election outcomes.
22:836:55223:29:14:109:520:482:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:Table 2 shows the OLS estimates of the coefficients in regression (12) including
22:837:55303:14:15:91:519:468:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the fixed effects and all the controls.  The first column pools all types of elections,
22:838:55390:15:14:91:519:453:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:while columns (2) through (6) include respectively Presidential, Senate, House and
22:839:55472:14:15:91:519:439:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Gubernatorial.   Both  specifications  (4)  and  (5)  focus  on  House  elections,  but  re-
22:840:55564:15:14:91:519:424:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:gression (4) uses the share of votes to the Republicans as dependent variable, while
22:841:55648:14:14:91:519:410:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:regression (5) uses the percentage of seats won by the Republicans.  Table 3 shows
22:842:55730:14:15:91:519:396:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the  same  estimates  based  on  the  2SLS  strategy.   Three  results  emerge.   First,  the
22:843:55823:15:14:91:519:381:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:impact of the share of immigrants on Republican votes is negative in all estimates
22:844:55905:14:15:91:519:367:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:but for one type of election (Gubernatorial).  Second, the negative estimates are sig-
22:845:55991:15:14:91:519:352:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:nificant in both OLS and IV specifications only for the House elections, while for the
22:846:56077:14:15:91:519:338:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:other elections the effects are not robust.  Third the negative significant estimates in
22:847:56165:15:14:91:519:323:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the IV are larger than in the OLS, which indicates the presence of omitted variables
22:848:56249:14:15:91:519:309:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that, at the same time, increase immigration and the share of the Republican vote.
22:849:56331:15:14:91:519:294:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Such  omitted  variables  could  be  economic  shocks  that  increase  local  business  in-
22:850:56422:14:14:91:519:280:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:come – immigrants are attracted by booming states and higher income is associated
22:851:56503:14:15:91:519:266:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:with Republican votes – or demographic shifts of the local population – aging local
22:852:56586:15:29:91:503:251:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:population create more jobs for immigrants and more votes for the Republicans.
22:853:56664:29:14:109:520:222:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:Concerning the control variables the results show that, on average, states with a
22:854:56745:14:15:91:519:208:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:higher share of high-school dropouts (the omitted reference group of education) tend
22:855:56829:15:14:91:519:193:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:to have a lower Republican vote share (the significance level varies across types of
22:856:56913:14:15:91:519:179:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:elections).  The average income of voters does not have a significant impact in any
22:857:56996:15:14:91:519:164:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:type of election.  Finally, states with higher unemployment rates are more likely to
22:858:57080:14:0:91:519:150:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:vote Democrat.  Overall, these results are in line with the findings of the literature
23:859:57168:0:15:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:on the determinants of elections and specifically similar to Della Vigna and Kaplan
23:860:57251:15:29:91:127:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:(2007).
23:861:57258:29:14:109:520:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:So, to a first inspection, the overall share of immigrants has a strong and quan-
23:862:57339:14:15:91:519:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:titatively large negative correlation with the share of Republican votes and the IV
23:863:57422:15:14:91:519:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:estimates suggest that such correlation is consistent with a negative causal effect.  An
23:864:57510:14:15:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:increase of immigrants by one percentage point of adult population is associated, in
23:865:57594:15:14:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the House elections, with a decrease of the Republican vote share of 1.36 percentage
23:866:57678:14:15:91:519:569:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:points, which is not significantly different from 1.  Such a large and negative coeffi-
23:867:57765:15:14:91:519:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:cient is consistent with a situation in which the direct effect of citizen immigrants is
23:868:57853:14:14:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:negative and strong and the indirect effect either works in the same direction as the
23:869:57938:14:15:91:519:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:direct one, or does not favor Republicans enough to offset the direct effect.  In order
23:870:58025:15:14:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:to analyze those effects in more detail, we turn next to estimating an equation that
23:871:58109:14:35:91:394:497:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:includes, separately, the variables considered by our model.
23:872:58169:35:22:91:393:462:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:5.2    The model-based estimating equation
23:873:58211:22:15:91:519:440:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:In this section we bring to the data, respectively, the linear and the linear-quadratic
23:874:58298:15:14:91:519:425:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:specifications  we  derived  from  the  model.   We  first  estimate  the  models  with  all
23:875:58390:14:14:91:519:411:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:elections  pooled  and,  next,  we  focus  on  House  elections,  which  are  the  only  ones
23:876:58483:14:15:91:519:397:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:where  we  found  a  significant  correlation  on  average  between  the  immigrant  share
23:877:58573:15:29:91:474:382:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:and the Republican vote share, both in the OLS and in the IV regressions.
23:878:58646:29:14:109:520:353:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:In the linear specification (8), the coefficientβ1represents the indirect political
23:879:58729:14:15:91:519:339:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:effect of immigration, which works through the impact of the non-citizen immigrant
23:880:58811:15:14:91:519:324:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:share.   The  empirical  evidence  from  some  European  countries  (see  Barone  et  al.
23:881:58900:14:15:91:519:310:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:(2014),  Halla  et  al.  (2012)  and  Otto  and  Steinhardt  (2014))  –  where  the  indirect
23:882:58993:15:14:91:519:295:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:political effect of migration is more relevant than the direct one, as naturalization
23:883:59078:14:14:91:519:281:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:rates tend to be small – suggests that natives become more politically conservative
23:884:59161:14:15:91:519:267:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:when migration increases.  If a similar effect takes place in the United States,  the
23:885:59246:15:14:91:519:252:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Republican vote share should increase when the fraction of non-citizen immigrants
23:886:59327:14:15:91:520:238:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:goes up, in which case we expectβ1>0.  If, on the other hand, the indirect effect is
23:887:59411:15:14:91:519:223:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:not very strong on average in the U.S., we may observeβ1= 0.  Alternatively, the
23:888:59491:14:15:91:519:209:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:indirect political effect may become relevant only for high values of the non-citizen
23:889:59576:15:14:91:519:194:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:immigrant  share,  given  that  only  then  immigration  becomes  a  visible  and  salient
23:890:59666:14:15:91:519:180:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:political issue for voters.  If this is the case, in specification (9) we should estimate a
23:891:59757:15:14:91:520:165:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:zero or negative linear term and a positive quadratic, namelyβL<= 0 andβQ>0,
23:892:59833:14:0:91:519:151:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:so that a higher share of non-citizen immigrants produces a boost to the Republican
24:893:59918:0:29:91:384:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:vote only when non-citizen immigrants are a large group.
24:894:59974:29:10:109:520:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:In both specifications (8) and (9), the coefficientβ2on the variablecmvoteshit=
24:895:60053:10:9:92:113:646:8:g_d0_f8:6:g_d0_f11:F:CMit
24:896:60057:9:10:97:520:637:8:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f1:A:Vitrepresents the direct political effect of migration, i.e.  the difference in average
24:897:60144:10:15:91:519:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:voting propensity for the Republican party between naturalized immigrants and na-
24:898:60225:15:14:91:519:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:tives.  According to anecdotal evidence (see for example the citation at the beginning
24:899:60311:14:15:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of the paper), naturalized immigrants in the U.S. tend to vote for the Democratic
24:900:60392:15:29:91:302:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:party.  Thus we expect to observeβ2<0.
24:901:60430:29:14:109:520:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:Finally note that,  in the empirical analysis below,  we will focus on regressions
24:902:60512:14:14:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that  either  pool  all  election  types  or  that  focus  on  House  elections,  for  which  we
24:903:60608:14:15:91:519:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:found the most robust results.  One possible explanation of the latter findings is the
24:904:60694:15:14:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:following.  In Presidential, Gubernatorial and Senate elections, very few candidates
24:905:60778:14:15:91:519:497:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:are up for vote – this is of course true in Presidential elections for which there is only
24:906:60868:15:14:91:519:482:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:one candidate per party common to all states, while in the other elections there are
24:907:60952:14:15:91:519:468:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:either one (Gubernational) or two (Senate) candidates per party in each state.  As a
24:908:61036:15:14:91:519:453:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:result, Presidential, Gubernatorial and Senate election campaigns are more focused
24:909:61118:14:15:91:519:439:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:on the program of the individual candidate rather than on the party program and,
24:910:61198:15:14:91:519:424:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:importantly, the individual candidate’s program may differ from his/her party’s one
24:911:61281:14:14:91:519:410:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:in relation to migration.  On the contrary, in House elections, there are many seats
24:912:61365:14:15:91:519:396:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:in each state – in the case of California, there are 53 seats – and therefore as many
24:913:61450:15:14:91:519:381:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:candidates for each party and state.  Voters may not be as aware of the individual
24:914:61532:14:15:91:519:367:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:candidate’s program and will likely vote based on the party’s political agenda.  This
24:915:61617:15:14:91:519:352:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:suggests that House elections may be more affected by the overall program of each
24:916:61698:14:10:91:519:338:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:party and may face less noise due to the individual program of the various candidates.
24:917:61784:10:54:91:99:328:8:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f3:F:21
24:918:61786:54:22:91:289:274:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:5.3    Instrumental Variables

25:948:63510:15:14:91:519:380:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the share of immigrants – from that country present in the state – because of mobility

25:951:63766:14:15:91:519:337:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:origin.  Hence preferences of early settlers which threaten the exclusion restriction –
25:952:63853:15:14:91:519:322:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:they may have been correlated with economic and political characteristics of a state
25:953:63937:14:29:91:447:308:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:and be persistent over time – do not play any role in this instrument.
25:954:64007:29:14:109:520:279:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:Separately we proxy non-citizen immigrants with another novel instrument.  A
25:955:64083:14:15:91:519:265:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:large part of those immigrants in the last two decades is represented by the group

26:998:66868:33:15:109:520:229:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:wherêNitis defined as in (14).  The instrument defined in (21) proxies the change
26:999:66950:15:14:91:519:214:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:in non-citizen immigrants in a state using the imputed inflow of undocumented based
26:1000:67033:14:19:91:519:200:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:on the total inflows (as inferred from apprehensions) and the proximity to the Mex-
26:1001:67116:19:15:101:519:181:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:23While not all undocumented immigrants enter through the Mexican border, as some of them
26:1002:67205:15:12:91:519:166:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:overstay  their  visa,  about  80%  of  undocumented  immigrants  are  Mexican  or  Central  American.
26:1003:67307:12:0:91:272:154:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:Hence our strategy focuses on this group.
27:1004:67350:0:15:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:ican border.  This variable may capture only a part of changes in non-citizen immi-
27:1005:67433:15:14:91:519:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:grants, however if that part is a significant part of the overall changes, this strategy
27:1006:67521:14:15:91:519:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:provides a novel way to analyze the potential impact of the yearly flows of undocu-
27:1007:67604:15:14:91:519:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:mented, and their presence across states, on the vote of U.S. citizens.  Finally, as an
27:1008:67691:14:15:91:519:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:instrument for the square of the share of non-citizen immigrants, we simply square
27:1009:67773:15:34:91:351:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the instrument of the non-citizen immigrant share.
27:1010:67823:34:23:91:216:578:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:5.4    Main results
27:1011:67842:23:14:91:519:555:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Using both OLS and IV, we estimate a significant negative effect of immigrants on
27:1012:67923:14:14:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the  Republican  vote  share  through  the  vote  of  citizen  immigrants.   As  discussed
27:1013:68013:14:15:91:519:527:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:above, this result is consistent with anecdotal evidence and could be explained by
27:1014:68095:15:14:91:519:512:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the fact that naturalized migrants favor a more open migration policy which would
27:1015:68176:14:15:91:519:498:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:allow them to be joined by family members abroad.  An alternative explanation is
27:1016:68256:15:14:91:519:483:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that migrants are often from countries where many political parties are to the left of
27:1017:68342:14:15:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Democrats and few are as socially conservative as Republicans, thus they are voting
27:1018:68425:15:29:91:341:454:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:for the same type of ideology they grew up with.
27:1019:68473:29:14:109:520:425:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:We also find evidence of non-linear effects of the population share of non-citizen
27:1020:68555:14:14:91:519:411:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:immigrants so that the marginal impact of new immigrants on the Republican vote
27:1021:68634:14:15:91:519:397:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:turns positive when the share is very high,  i.e.  when recent immigration becomes
27:1022:68716:15:14:91:520:382:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:a salient feature at the polls.24Columns (1) through (3) in Table 4 show the OLS
27:1023:68796:14:15:91:519:368:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:estimates  corresponding  to  the  linear  specification  using  data  for,  respectively,  all
27:1024:68891:15:14:91:519:353:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:elections (regression (1)) and House elections (regressions (2) and (3)).  Columns (4)
27:1025:68977:14:15:91:519:339:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:and (5) present the OLS estimates of the quadratic specification for House elections.
27:1026:69062:15:14:91:519:324:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:While the coefficient on the share of citizen immigrants is very significant and neg-
27:1027:69147:14:15:91:519:310:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:ative in all specifications, the impact of the share of non-citizen immigrants is small
27:1028:69234:15:14:91:519:295:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:and negative or non significant when entered linearly, but has a significant convex
27:1029:69317:14:29:91:292:281:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:effect when entered as linear-quadratic.
27:1030:69357:29:14:109:520:252:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:Table 5 focuses on House elections only and shows the 2SLS estimates for the
27:1031:69433:14:15:91:519:238:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:linear specification (columns (1) and (2)) and for the linear-quadratic specification
27:1032:69518:15:14:91:519:223:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:(columns (3) and (4)).  The top panel of Table 5 shows the second-stage estimates,
27:1033:69600:14:15:91:519:209:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:while the bottom panel shows the first-stage estimates.  At the bottom of the top
27:1034:69681:15:18:91:519:194:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:panel, we include the Kleibergen-Paap F statistic, which provides an indication of
27:1035:69763:18:15:101:519:176:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:24Note  that  this  result  is  consistent  with  the  finding  in  Baerg  et  al.  (2014),  that  the  negative
27:1036:69875:15:12:91:519:161:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:reaction  in  terms  of  Democratic  votes  to  the  presence  of  unauthorized  immigrants  is  strongest
27:1037:69981:12:0:91:296:149:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:when this presence reaches a certain threshold.
28:1038:70030:0:15:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the significance of the instrument.  Note that since our estimation includes robust
28:1039:70113:15:14:91:519:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:standard errors, the standard critical values of Stock-Yogo do not apply (Stock and
28:1040:70196:14:15:91:519:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Yogo (2002)).  Due to the lack of alternative critical values, we apply the same rule
28:1041:70281:15:14:91:519:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of thumb as suggested by Stock and Yogo, i.e.  an F-statistic above 10 indicates that
28:1042:70366:14:15:91:519:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the IV is acceptable.  In addition, we also test for the joint significance of endogenous
28:1043:70455:15:14:91:519:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:regressors by including the Anderson Rubin Wald test.  A p-value above 0.1 indicates
28:1044:70539:14:15:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that we cannot reject the null hypothesis that the instruments are jointly insignificant
28:1045:70627:15:29:91:363:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:and thus robust to the presence of weak instruments.
28:1046:70679:29:14:109:520:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:One result stands out.  In each specification and for each method of estimation we
28:1047:70761:14:14:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:find strong evidence of the negative effect of citizen immigrants on the Republican
28:1048:70844:14:15:91:519:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:vote share. Specifically, we estimate a negative and significant value for the coefficient
28:1049:70934:15:14:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f1:B:β2in all regressions.  Using the share of Republican votes in the House elections, the
28:1050:71020:14:15:91:519:497:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:point estimate in Table 5 is 1.75 and 1.81, but not significantly different from one
28:1051:71104:15:14:91:519:482:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:(because of the large standard error).  An increase in immigrant citizens as a share of
28:1052:71191:14:15:91:519:468:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:voters by one percentage point decreases the share of the Republican vote by 1.75 to
28:1053:71275:15:14:91:519:453:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:1.81 percentage points.  As for the indirect political effect of immigration, when we
28:1054:71360:14:15:91:519:439:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:model the impact of the variableNCMitMit+Nitas linear, in specification (8), the estimated
28:1055:71450:15:14:91:519:424:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:coefficient is negative and (marginally) significant in column (1) but insignificant in
28:1056:71537:14:14:91:519:410:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:column (2).  However, in the non-linear specification, the impact of the non-citizen
28:1057:71621:14:15:91:519:396:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:immigrant share is significant with a negative linear effect and a positive quadratic
28:1058:71706:15:14:91:519:381:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:effect, hence it is clearly convex.  This implies that, while at low values of the share
28:1059:71794:14:15:91:519:367:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of  non-citizen  immigrants,  their  impact  on  the  share  of  Republican  votes  is  likely
28:1060:71888:15:14:91:519:352:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:non-significant  or  even  negative,  for  high  values  of  that  share  their  impact  turns
28:1061:71982:14:15:91:519:338:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:positive.  Such a convex relation between the share of non-citizen immigrants and
28:1062:72063:15:14:91:519:323:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the Republican vote share suggests that the perceptions of new migrants affect voters’
28:1063:72149:14:15:91:519:309:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:behavior only when their share is large and their presence is rather conspicuous.  In
28:1064:72234:15:14:91:519:294:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the next section, we will show the relation between the marginal effect of the non-
28:1065:72317:14:14:91:519:280:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:citizen share on Republican votes and the initial share and calculate the threshold
28:1066:72400:14:29:91:293:266:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:value at which the effect turns positive.
28:1067:72441:29:15:109:520:237:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:Thus  the  results  in  Table  5  emphasize  the  different  effect  of  citizens  and  non-
28:1068:72533:15:14:91:519:222:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:citizen immigrants.  In Tables 2 and 3 we detected an overall negative association
28:1069:72615:14:15:91:519:208:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:between immigrants and Republican votes.  However, the estimates in Tables 4 and
28:1070:72695:15:14:91:519:193:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:5 provide a more complex picture of the political impact of migration to the U.S..
28:1071:72777:14:15:91:519:179:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:We  find  that,  while  the  share  of  citizen  immigrants  is  a  significant  boost  to  the
28:1072:72872:15:14:91:519:164:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Democratic party, the effect of non-citizen immigrants is somewhat more complex and
28:1073:72955:14:0:91:519:150:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:non-linear.  In particular new immigrants, who are mainly non-citizen immigrants,
29:1074:73038:0:15:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:have  a  negative  or  non-significant  effect  on  the  Republican  vote  share  when  their
29:1075:73131:15:14:91:519:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:share  is  low,  but  a  positive  one  at  higher  values  of  that  share.   These  results  are
29:1076:73229:14:15:91:519:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:consistent  with  naturalized  migrants  being  less  likely  to  vote  for  the  Republican
29:1077:73321:15:14:91:519:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:party than native voters and with citizens’ political preferences moving towards the
29:1078:73405:14:15:91:519:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Republican party because of high immigration, i.e.  when migration is supposedly a
29:1079:73487:15:40:91:241:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:salient issue in voters’ minds.
29:1080:73518:40:26:91:342:572:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:6    Effect of Different Policies
29:1081:73551:26:14:91:519:546:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:To illustrate the implications of these estimates, it is useful to calculate how these
29:1082:73637:14:15:91:519:532:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:coefficients map into the effects of changes in different types of immigrants on the
29:1083:73721:15:14:91:519:517:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:share of Republican votes.  Using the estimated coefficients of the linear specification
29:1084:73809:14:15:91:520:503:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:in Table 5 (βL=−0.80 andβ2=−1.81), we can evaluate which one of the following
29:1085:73886:15:29:91:434:488:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:policies is most beneficial/harmful for the Republican vote share25.
29:1086:73954:29:14:109:520:459:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:1)Increase in newly arrived immigrants:An inflow of new immigrants, typically
29:1087:74031:14:15:91:519:445:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:entering the U.S. without citizenship rights (hence as non-citizens), by 1 percent of
29:1088:74116:15:14:91:520:430:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the population will have an impact equal toβLon the Republican share of votes. This
29:1089:74199:14:14:91:519:416:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:could be driven by a more open immigration policy that admits extra immigrants.
29:1090:74278:14:15:91:520:402:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:The negative estimate ofβLimplies that, on average, the republican party will loose
29:1091:74361:15:14:91:519:387:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:0.8 percent of the votes per percentage point increase.  However, once we recognize
29:1092:74444:14:15:91:519:373:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the salient feature of non-citizen immigration, the impact on the republican vote can
29:1093:74529:15:14:91:519:358:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:turn positive.  Given our estimates in Table 5, column 3, the marginal effect of a 1
29:1094:74613:14:15:91:520:344:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:percent increase of non-citizen immigrants equalsβL+ 2βQNCMitNit+Mit.  It is positive for
29:1095:74702:15:14:91:519:329:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:values above 13.2%.  Figure 4 illustrate the dependence of this effect on the share
29:1096:74785:14:15:91:519:315:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of  non-citizen  immigrants.   As  of  the  last  presidential  election,  in  2012,  6  states
29:1097:74880:15:14:91:519:300:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:(California,  District of Columbia,  Nevada,  New Jersey,  New York and Texas) had
29:1098:74962:14:14:91:519:286:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:values larger than this threshold.  At the congressional-district level, using estimates
29:1099:75050:14:15:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of the non-citizen migrant share based on the American Community Survey for the
29:1100:75129:15:14:91:519:257:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:114th Congress, we find that for 55 out of 434 congressional districts the impact of
29:1101:75213:14:15:91:519:243:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the above share is positive.  For 26 districts the effect is not significantly different
29:1102:75301:15:14:91:519:228:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:from zero and for the remaining 353 the effect is negative, see Figure 7(a).  Figure
29:1103:75385:14:15:91:519:214:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:7(b) plots the geographical distribution of the impact on the Republican vote share
29:1104:75468:15:14:91:520:199:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:for  each  Congressional-district  using  (βL=−4.29,βQ=  16.27  andβ2=−1.75).
29:1105:75545:14:18:91:519:185:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Hence for the majority of states and congressional districts,  the potential positive
29:1106:75630:18:15:101:519:167:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:25The detailed derivation of the marginal effects of each policy, using the definition of the variables
29:1107:75733:15:0:91:282:152:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:and shares, can be found in the Appendix 9
30:1108:75777:0:15:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:effect of new immigration on the Republican share does not occur at their current
30:1109:75858:15:29:91:252:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:level of non-citizen immigrants.

30:1134:76694:29:15:109:520:472:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:3)Pure  Scale  effect:This is an increase (decrease) in the total number of im-

30:1144:77178:13:17:423:519:395:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:on the share of the
30:1145:77197:17:15:91:519:378:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Republican vote.  Using the estimates from Table 5, this marginal effect is negative
30:1146:77281:15:28:91:226:363:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:for any U.S. state in 2012.
30:1147:77308:28:15:109:520:335:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:Summarizing the main results,  we can emphasize three findings.  First,  all our
30:1148:77388:15:14:91:519:320:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:estimates suggest that an increase in the share of naturalized immigrants increases
30:1149:77471:14:15:91:519:306:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:significantly the share of vote to the democratic party.  This may be because they
30:1150:77553:15:14:91:519:291:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:tend to vote for the Democratic party more intensively than natives (which is the
30:1151:77634:14:15:91:519:277:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:explanation suggested by our framework) but we cannot rule out that part of the
30:1152:77713:15:14:91:519:262:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:effect proceeds from increases democratic preferences of natives in response to more
30:1153:77797:14:15:91:519:248:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:naturalized immigrants.  Second, our findings also indicate that when the share of
30:1154:77879:15:14:91:519:233:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:non-citizen immigrants is large, further increases in the non-citizen migrants share
30:1155:77963:14:14:91:519:219:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:can  increase  the  share  of  votes  to  the  Republicans.   Through  this  channel,  large
30:1156:78055:14:15:91:519:205:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:populations of new immigrants (or non-citizen immigrants) in a state might increase
30:1157:78138:15:14:91:519:190:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the chances of electoral success of the Republican party, when the share of non-citizen
30:1158:78225:14:15:91:519:176:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:migrants is high.  As these immigrants do not vote, the effect we identify is consistent
30:1159:78313:15:14:91:519:161:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:with  the  idea  that  voters’  preferences  can  be  moved  towards  a  more  conservative
30:1160:78404:14:0:91:519:147:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:immigration stand, especially in the House elections, when these immigrants become
31:1161:78488:0:15:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:a large and noticeable presence in the state.  Third, and final, such adverse electoral
31:1162:78575:15:14:91:519:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:response to non-citizen immigrants is relevant only at very high population shares of
31:1163:78660:14:15:91:519:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:non-citizen immigrants, which in 2012 only characterized 12% of electoral districts.
31:1164:78744:15:14:91:519:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:If we focus on the combined effect through both channels, we now estimate it to be
31:1165:78826:14:15:91:519:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:negative in all districts.  However,  it is important to understand that this average
31:1166:78911:15:14:91:519:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:impact is the outcome of two opposing effects and that the relative strength of the
31:1167:78994:14:15:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:latter ones could change over time and reverse the sign of the combined effect.  In
31:1168:79077:15:14:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:particular,  to  the  extent  that  the  indirect  effect  is  considered  as  the  relevant  one,
31:1169:79175:14:15:91:519:569:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:when discussing how the presence of undocumented immigrants may affect the vote
31:1170:79254:15:14:91:519:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of citizens, our mechanism may rationalize the frequent attempt of some republican
31:1171:79336:14:14:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:candidates to make this a salient issue for the elections.  However, we also estimate
31:1172:79421:14:15:91:519:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that the effect on Republican vote share in response to undocumented immigrants
31:1173:79500:15:40:91:315:511:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:would be positive only in very few districts.
31:1174:79545:40:30:91:198:471:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:7    Channels
31:1175:79558:30:22:91:519:441:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:F:7.1    Labor-market, welfare-state and non-economic channels
31:1176:79618:22:14:91:519:419:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Our empirical results so far show that, on average, an increase of the share of non-

32:1221:81252:15:14:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of immigrants to a stronger extent,  the less educated they are.  Thus,  an increase

32:1223:81421:15:14:91:519:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:migration, i.e.  the Republican party, more in states with a large population of low
32:1224:81505:14:14:91:520:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:educated (see columns 1 to 10 in Table 6 –βLCis significant in columns 1,3,4,5,9 and
32:1225:81589:14:15:91:519:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:10).  We also find evidence that,  controlling for education (share of low educated)
32:1226:81673:15:14:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:in states where voters are richer, an increase in the share of non-citizen immigrants
32:1227:81758:14:15:91:519:497:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:increases the Republican vote share. This result is consistent with a rational response
32:1228:81845:15:14:91:519:482:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of citizens to welfare-state channel under the tax-adjustment model (Facchini and
32:1229:81926:14:15:91:519:468:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Mayda (2009)).  Non-citizen immigrants are (relatively) poor27, thus they are likely
32:1230:82010:15:14:91:519:453:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:perceived as a fiscal burden,  being on the receiving end of the welfare state.  The
32:1231:82094:14:15:91:519:439:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:tax adjustment model assumes that the welfare state adjusts to migration through a
32:1232:82176:15:14:91:519:424:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:change in tax rates.  Given that migrants are poorer than voters, they give rise to a
32:1233:82261:14:14:91:519:410:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:deficit in the government’s budget constraint, which in the tax-adjustment model is
32:1234:82344:14:15:91:519:396:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:brought back to balance through an increase in tax rates.  Higher tax rates hurt all
32:1235:82428:15:14:91:519:381:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:voters, but rich ones to a greater extent (because of progressive taxes).  Therefore,
32:1236:82513:14:15:91:519:367:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:through the welfare-state channel under the tax adjustment model, we should find
32:1237:82593:15:14:91:519:352:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that in states where voters are richer, an increase in the share of non-citizen migrants
32:1238:82681:14:15:91:520:338:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:should  increase  the  Republican  vote  share.   Our  results  in  Table  6,  (βW C>0  in
32:1239:82771:15:14:91:519:323:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:all  regressions  and  significant  in  columns  1,2,4,6,  7  and  8)  is  consistent  with  this
32:1240:82868:14:15:91:519:309:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:explanation.  Finally the negative and significant estimate of the main effect of the
32:1241:82953:15:14:91:519:294:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:variable “Share of non-citizen immigrants” on the share of republican vote implies
32:1242:83035:14:14:91:519:280:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that, in states where voters are relatively skilled and low income, the impact of the
32:1243:83120:14:15:91:520:266:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:non-citizen migrant share on Republican votes is negative and significant (β1<0).
32:1244:83201:15:14:91:519:251:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:This is again consistent with both the labor-market channel and with the welfare-
32:1245:83282:14:15:91:519:237:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:state channel under the tax adjustment model.  Educated voters do not perceive to
32:1246:83363:15:14:91:519:222:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:be in competition with immigrants in the labor market and, if their income os not
32:1247:83444:14:18:91:519:208:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:too high, they will not be as affected by increases in tax rates.  Thus the response of
32:1248:83531:18:16:101:519:190:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:26Over the considered period, the average number of years of education of non-citizens immigrants
32:1249:83628:16:8:91:320:174:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:was 12.6 while it was 14.1 for the voting population.
32:1250:83681:8:16:101:519:166:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:27In the period we analyze, the average income at constant 1999 prices is 25614 USD for non-
32:1251:83773:16:0:91:386:150:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:citizen migrants compared to 34228 USD for the voting population.
33:1252:83840:0:15:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:skilled and lower income voters to immigrants will decrease the electoral success of
33:1253:83924:15:14:91:519:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the Republican party. All these results, on both economic channels, produce a picture
33:1254:84009:14:15:91:519:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of the perceived economic impact of migration which matches well the evidence from
33:1255:84091:15:14:91:519:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the literature on individual attitudes towards immigrants (see Scheve and Slaughter
33:1256:84174:14:29:91:491:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:(2001), Hanson et al. (2007), Mayda (2006), and Facchini and Mayda (2009)).
33:1257:84249:29:15:109:520:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:Note that, at the individual level, skill and income tend to be positively correlated,
33:1258:84335:15:14:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:therefore  the  labor-market  and  welfare-state  channels  (under  the  tax-adjustment

33:1260:84506:15:14:91:519:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:nians will welcome non-citizen migrants, because of their (perceived) labor-market
33:1261:84588:14:14:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:effects,  and oppose them,  because of their (perceived) welfare-state effects.  These
33:1262:84674:14:15:91:519:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:effects working in opposite directions could explain why the impact of the non-citizen
33:1263:84760:15:29:91:431:511:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:migrant share is small or not significant in the linear specification.
33:1264:84830:29:14:109:520:482:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:Finally, we analyze the non-economic channel by introducing several measures of
33:1265:84909:14:15:91:519:468:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:cultural dissimilarity between immigrants and natives and interacting each of them
33:1266:84991:15:14:91:519:453:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:with the non-citizen migrant share.  The measures we consider focus on, respectively,
33:1267:85076:14:15:91:519:439:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:language,  religious  and  historical  differences  (see  columns  3  through  8,  Table  6)
33:1268:85168:15:14:91:519:424:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:–  by  historical  differences  we  mean  lack  of  a  common  colonial  relationship.   We
33:1269:85259:14:14:91:519:410:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:also  average  these  measures  into  a  composite  one  (see  columns  9  and  10).   The
33:1270:85349:14:15:91:519:396:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:different measures of cultural differences deliver the same message captured by the
33:1271:85432:15:14:91:520:381:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:coefficientβNE, which is always positive and often significant:  Cultural dissimilarity
33:1272:85519:14:15:91:519:367:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:with immigrants pushes votes to the Republican party, the higher is the non-citizen
33:1273:85602:15:34:91:165:352:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:migrant share.
33:1274:85616:34:23:91:278:318:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:7.2    Participation channel
33:1275:85644:23:14:91:519:295:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Immigrants may also affect the decision of voters to participate in an election, par-
33:1276:85729:14:14:91:519:281:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:ticularly in states where the immigrant population changed a lot.  Some of the effects
33:1277:85815:14:15:91:519:267:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:attributed to the direct and indirect channel could be due to attracting or discour-
33:1278:85899:15:14:91:519:252:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:aging some marginal voters.  In particular if the main effect of citizen immigrants
33:1279:85982:14:15:91:519:238:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:is  their  own  vote,  while  the  main  impact  of  non-citizen  immigrants  is  in  altering
33:1280:86076:15:14:91:519:223:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the  vote  behavior  of  citizens  we  should  observe  such  differential  impact  on  voting
33:1281:86170:14:15:91:519:209:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:turnout.  For this reason,  we consider an additional specification,  where we inves-
33:1282:86255:15:14:91:519:194:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:tigate the impact of citizen and non-citizen immigrants on the voter turnout.  We
33:1283:86336:14:15:91:519:180:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:expect  that,  as  the  share  of  non-citizen  immigrants  increases,  their  indirect  effect
33:1284:86431:15:14:91:519:165:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:may become stronger as they affect voter’s turnout.  To the contrary the presence
33:1285:86512:14:0:91:519:151:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of citizen immigrants should not affect citizens turnout much.  To shed light on this
34:1286:86599:0:32:91:339:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:hypothesis, we estimate the following regression:
34:1287:86648:32:0:168:266:653:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:?:V Tit=si+qt+βL
34:1288:86662:0:16:273:311:661:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:?:NCMit
34:1289:86667:16:0:267:317:645:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:?:Mit+Nit
34:1290:86674:0:0:322:344:653:12:g_d0_f1:8:g_d0_f3:?:+β2
34:1291:86677:0:16:346:372:661:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:?:CMit
34:1292:86681:16:0:353:366:645:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:?:Vit
34:1293:86684:0:26:377:520:653:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:+βxXit+εit(22)
34:1294:86698:26:14:109:520:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:where the dependent variable, Voter TurnoutV Titin stateiat timet, is defined
34:1295:86775:14:15:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:as the ratio of the number of actual votes divided by the eligible voting population.
34:1296:86860:15:14:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Note that the eligible voting population excludes non-citizen immigrants, prisoners,
34:1297:86944:14:15:91:519:584:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:people on probation as well as people on parole from the voting age population, i.e.
34:1298:87028:15:14:91:519:569:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:everyone residing in the United States, age 18 and older, as defined by the Census
34:1299:87110:14:15:91:520:555:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Bureau.28The  independent  regressors  are  the  same  variables  as  in  the  previous
34:1300:87197:15:14:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:regression specification.  To account for the endogeneity of immigration on election
34:1301:87281:14:29:91:340:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:participation, we estimate equation 22 via 2SLS.
34:1302:87329:29:14:109:520:497:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:The results in Table 7 show the linear and non-linear results.  In the linear speci-
34:1303:87413:14:15:91:519:483:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:fication, Column (1), voter turnout increases in the share of non-citizen immigrants
34:1304:87497:15:14:91:519:468:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:by 0.8 percent, while the effect of citizen immigrants is not significant.  Turning the
34:1305:87584:14:15:91:519:454:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:attention to the non-linear specification, the results in Column (2) show that non-
34:1306:87667:15:14:91:519:439:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:citizen immigrants increase the voter turnout at a declining rate.  Figure 6 plots the
34:1307:87753:14:15:91:519:425:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:marginal effects of 1 percentage point increase of the share of non-citizen immigrants
34:1308:87839:15:14:91:519:410:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:on  the  Voter  Turnout.   In  the  case  of  California,  the  state  with  the  highest  share
34:1309:87935:14:15:91:519:396:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of non-citizen immigrants in the year 2012 (18%), the marginal effect can even be
34:1310:88016:15:14:91:519:381:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:negative.  On the other hand, in all other states the share of non-citizen immigrants
34:1311:88101:14:14:91:519:367:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:has a positive impact on voters participation.  Overall, our results are consistent with
34:1312:88189:14:15:91:519:353:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the view that higher shares of non-citizen immigrants spur election participation of
34:1313:88273:15:40:91:467:338:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:natives, while having no effect on the participation of citizen immigrants.
34:1314:88348:40:26:91:213:298:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:8    Conclusion
34:1315:88363:26:15:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Looking at the debate surrounding immigration policy reform in the U.S., one mes-
34:1316:88444:15:14:91:519:257:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:sage  is  clear:   For  the  most  part  Republicans  are  hesitant  to  push  forward  with
34:1317:88536:14:14:91:519:243:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:migration policy reforms, especially those that would give a path to citizenship to
34:1318:88619:14:15:91:519:229:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:currently undocumented immigrants.  In addition, in electoral times, their average
34:1319:88701:15:14:91:519:214:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:attitude towards migrants is to talk “tough” about the presence of undocumented
34:1320:88780:14:15:91:519:200:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:immigrants.  In this paper, we analyze the impact of immigrants on the vote to the
34:1321:88862:15:18:91:519:185:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Republican party and find some regularities that may help understand this politi-
34:1322:88943:18:15:101:519:167:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:28The voter turnout is public available data compiled by McDonald (2002) and freely available
34:1323:89036:15:0:91:234:152:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:at http://www.electproject.org/.
35:1324:89070:0:15:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:cal behavior.  Political analysts often refer to the pro-Democrat electoral behavior of
35:1325:89157:15:14:91:519:670:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:naturalized immigrants (and second-generation ones) to explain the reluctance of the
35:1326:89241:14:15:91:519:656:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Republican Party to push forward with migration policy reform.  However, we note
35:1327:89321:15:14:91:519:641:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that this view is inconsistent with recent research based on European data showing
35:1328:89403:14:15:91:519:627:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:that,  actually,  high immigrant shares might be driving votes towards conservative
35:1329:89486:15:14:91:519:612:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:parties, which promise a reduction in immigration.  We shed light on the difference
35:1330:89569:14:15:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:between the European findings and the views of U.S. political analysts by separately
35:1331:89653:15:29:91:373:583:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:considering two groups of immigrants and their effects.
35:1332:89708:29:14:109:520:554:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:A:Our  results  lead  us  to  two  conclusions.   First,  non-citizen/undocumented  im-
35:1333:89793:14:14:91:519:540:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:migrants are both the enemy and the raison d’ˆetre of some politicians:  right-wing
35:1334:89876:14:15:91:519:526:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:parties  in  Europe  and  vocal  anti-immigration  Republicans  in  the  U.S.  flourish  in
35:1335:89967:15:14:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:localities and times characterized by high non-citizen immigrant share.  Focusing on
35:1336:90051:14:15:91:519:497:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:the U.S., Republicans can gain votes from (non-citizen/undocumented) migrants as
35:1337:90131:15:14:91:519:482:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:their presence seem to make U.S. citizen voters more conservative.  Second, the latter
35:1338:90217:14:15:91:519:468:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:finding is consistent with Republicans talking tough about migration during electoral
35:1339:90302:15:14:91:519:453:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:times.  However we note that the political returns to talking tough on migration by
35:1340:90385:14:15:91:519:439:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Republicans may be limited since we find that the non-citizen migrant share has a
35:1341:90466:15:14:91:519:424:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:positive impact on Republicans’ political success only when this share is high, which
35:1342:90551:14:14:91:519:410:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:presumably  makes  the  topic  of  migration  salient  in  voters’  minds  or  increases  the
35:1343:90644:14:15:91:519:396:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:concern of citizens.  Based on data from 2012, the year of the last presidential elec-
35:1344:90730:15:14:91:519:381:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:tion, six states (California, District of Columbia, Nevada, New Jersey, New York and
35:1345:90814:14:15:91:519:367:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Texas) had values of the non-citizen migrant share high enough to make its impact
35:1346:90895:15:14:91:519:352:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:positive.   As  we  only  found  the  effect  to  be  present  in  House  elections,  however,
35:1347:90989:14:15:91:519:338:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:it is more meaningful to look at congressional districts, rather than states.  At the
35:1348:91074:15:14:91:519:323:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:Congressional-district level, using estimates of the non-citizen migrant share based
35:1349:91158:14:15:91:519:309:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:on the American Community Survey for the 114th Congress, we find that only 55 out
35:1350:91239:15:14:91:519:294:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:of 434 Congressional districts (less than 13% of them) had large enough non-citizen
35:1351:91322:14:0:91:395:280:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:B:share to produce a positive impact on the Republican vote.
